< review>
Impressions from 3 Singaporeans:
- Kaya toast was legit.
- Teh was OK. Not enough tea flavor, but at least it wasn't bitter, which happens if it's over-steeped. Could also taste the condensed milk.
- Nasi lemak: Rice tasted like coconut milk but was also far too sweet. I still enjoyed it though. Sambal and the other ingredients were mostly legit.
- Prata: they put spring onions on it for some reason, which overpowered the flavor of the prata.

Overall a relatively decent attempt at Singaporean food, considering the dearth of other good Singaporean restaurants.</review>

< text>
The Food
If you ever looked for Singaporean food in the bay area, you might realize Killiney Kopitiam is a popular choice. Probably also the closest genuine choice? (Don't get it confused with Kopitiam Cafe in Milpitas though.) I've been there a few times and compared it a bit to my experience in Singapore. Here's also some dishes I've tried
- Yuan Yang (w/Tea & Condense Milk)
- Kaya Toast
- Nasi Lemak
- Laksa
- Char Kway Teow
Most of the selection is pretty good, though I would say they are missing a bit of flare when compared to Singapore. But they still taste good with nice flavors. I would like to go back and try some of their other selection like Bak Kut Teh and Chicken and Rice. Whenever I go to Singapore, I must get Chicken and Rice!

The Miscellaneous
Killiney Kopitiam is on one of the main streets, but there is a decent amount of street parking. They seem to have opened recently, but haven't got a chance to use their inside, cause pandemic. They have takeout or outdoor seating, though your mileage may vary. They have a pretty good selection on their menu, covering most of the Singaporean dishes. Their service is also pretty friendly and sincere.</text>

It's got a "little of this, little of that" feel that's tends to result in overdone, overwrought dishes. The solution - bring the country to you! The dishes at Killiney Kopitiam are restrained and delicious.
Just be aware that as soy sauce is to chinese cooking and fish sauce to vietnamese and thai, is shrimp paste to singaporean... < Name>
Xinhong Lim</Name>
<time>1601959836364</time><rating>5<//rating><review>I'd say that this the most authentic tasting Singaporean food I've had from a restaurant in the Bay Area thus far. Killiney Kopitiam is a well-loved institution in Singapore, and as a food-crazy Singaporean, I'm so happy (even proud) to see them set up shop here. Mind you, there is no monolithic version of various Singaporean dishes and every restaurant has its own rendition, but I like Killiney's versions in Singapore and here. I seldom write reviews but felt compelled to do this one.

Stepping into the restaurant to place my order brought a tear to my eye, as the place smelt like a proper Singapore food court / Kopitiam (Coffeeshop) with its mixed aromas of Kopi (coffee), teh (tea), toast etc. I ordered several dishes: Roti Prata, Chicken curry, Mee Siam, Mee Rebus, Mee Siam, Seafood Bee Hoon, even iced Teh-C Siew Dai (tea with evaporated milk and less sugar). Tastes just like what I've eaten at the original Killiney Kopitiam(s) in Singapore. Tastes like home.

Mee siam:
Gravy tastes just like what Kiliney's sells, which is a bit in the thicker side of the spectrum of what one can find in Singapore, with more tamarind flavour and less coconut milk. The Bee Hoon (rice vermicelli or Á±≥Á≤â) is a bit thicker but that's consistent with Bee Hoon in general here.  That's mostly just texture anyway, the flavour is great. They even have chives and thin sliced tau kwa, which really completes it.

Mee rebus:
Tastes great, again just like what Killiney sells in Singapore. I prefer my mee rebus with a bit more ground nuts but that's just me. Certainly an authentic mee rebus. Not something I've really ever seen in any other restaurant here. Make sure you finish it with the provided kalamansi limes for max flavour! Could be enhanced even further with a drizzle of Kecap manis (dark sweet soy sauce) and julienned green chillies.

Char Kway Teow:
Pretty good, but somewhat lacking in wok hei (the blend of flavours emerging from the Maillard reaction and smoke as a result of rapid high heat wok cooking). The Kway Teow (thick rice noodles) was rather thicker than what one would typically get in Singapore, but had a good flavour.

Seafood Bee Hoon:
Highly recommended, better than their Char Kway Teow imho. Balance of flavours is good and the chef fried it well with some decent wok hei. Make sure you eat this piping hot for max effect.  Transported me back to a zi char (cooked food) stall in a Singapore Kopitiam.

Chicken curry:
Really good Nyonya style curry, more Singaporean-tasting than any other version I've eaten at any restaurant here. For the less initiated, this is quite different from Thai yellow curry or Jndian curries. I was hoping for a larger portion though, this is essentially an individual-sized portion, essentially one chicken drumstick and potatoes. Tastes just like what Kiliney sells. And it's actually different from curry sauce provided together with the Roti Prata. Killiney in Singapore sells the base sauce in foil packs for home cooks, and they should do so here too! (*hint hint Mr Woon*)

Roti Prata:
Tastes fragrant and light like a Kopitiam roti prata. Shiok and Indo restaurants in Menlo Park and Palo Alto make good roti pratas too, and Indo's may be a bit crispier than the one I got at Killiney. That could be because it was a bit cold by the time I brought Killiney's home. Killiney's also much cheaper than Indo's, $6 vs $9.

Mr Woon, the owner of the Killiney franchise in Singapore, is Hainanese, and the Killiney Kopitiams are typical Hainanese kopitiams. The Hainanese migrants to Singapore established themselves as formidable cooks serving under British colonists, and their cooking is a blend of Chinese, Malay, Indian and Western flavours (just like the melting pot of Singapore). This is reflected in the dishes on offer at Killiney (e.g. chicken curry - blend of Chinese/Malay/Indian, Hainanese pork cutlet - blend of Western/Chinese). Interesting factoid: many of Mr Woon's family members went to Stanford, so there's a Palo Alto connection here.</review><Pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipN38Q8i4VVjQjRVgnujBjW_UZADq4rRq967E6o=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipP2IuudvKbidZuM_PwfS64HeF1uTnsZ4bLBNFo=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNChrl8V4wXijykGUC91coWqQoT2wtZRuwhIX8=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOHMDTjjcCoaqBKtX7II4B29QJE7elEPacbGE4=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNoS19GfDQ26SPXVZRGiD8Rs_Ivkq7JA48v8CU=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNG6pL-edbZ6j4IDj4fG832B8ZEGUWlAQ2DDsU=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]</Pics>< Resp>

<Rating>5<//Rating>< text>
I've been wanting to check out this kopi tiam ever since they opened up, but only got a chance to do it yesterday. I've been to their original location, and although it's not as good as the ones in Singapore, I think their food and coffee are still pretty good, and definitely satisfy my cravings.

I ordered kaya toast, hainanese chicken rice, and kopi peng (iced coffee with condensed milk). I really enjoyed them all, and the chicken rice is comparable to the one I used to get in Singapore. The coffee was also good, but the kaya toast felt a bit off. I'm not sure how to put it, as it's not bad, but it just doesn't feel the same as the one I usually get.

The food is a bit pricey, but still worth it. When I was working in Singapore, I go to Killiney or other kopi tiam branches almost every day in the morning before work. Safe to say I won't be doing that here, even if it's close to my place.

All in all, it's definitely good enough to satisfy my craving for kopi team, something that the bay area has been missing all this time. I will definitely come back (just not too often).<//text>

5 stars for the food/staff and 4 for the wait.
Very good, authentic Singaporean food at reasonable prices for downtown Palo Alto.

Would recommend the nasi lemak and laksa. We wanted to try the bak kut teh and char kway teow but they were out of those dishes by the evening. Get there earlier for lunch if you want to avoid this!

Seems like they are still figuring things out and I hope they can have a system to notify us when our order is ready (text, email), since we wouldn't mind the wait as much if we could walk around downtown.

Will definitely come back and try again when ordering is a bit easier!</text>

<text>My mouth has suffered from "military dentistry" for much of my life, so I put up with an awful lot.  I don't think that I've ever heard of someone who ENJOYED going to have anything done.

That said, and in the midst of the shelter-in-place, I had a crown come off (from another dentist so long ago that I don't even remember the procedure, much less the dentist). < Review>
I think a sign of a good dentist is having a lot of hi-tech gadgets.  Not that the gadgets necessarily make for good dentistry, but I figure that if the dentist is worried about spending time and money to be on the leading edge in technology, they're likely also doing the same to be on the leading edge in dental practices.  Since I'm not a dentist and have no idea what the latest and greatest is in dental practices, I look instead for the tech (which I do know a little about!)

Dr. Fletcher has some great equipment.  Flat screen monitors everywhere, even over my head as I lie in the chair.  A digital X-Ray machine which immediately shows my teeth on that flat screen monitor over my head!  An optical digital camera he uses to show me what the new filling looks like!

What's more, Dr. Fletcher and his staff are really friendly.  I was waiting in the lobby this morning with my kids while my wife was getting a filling, and mentioned to the receptionist that I thought I had lost a filling recently.  She got me in for a same-day afternoon appointment to have Dr. Fletcher look at it.  When he heard about it, he told her he might as well have a look at it immediately--save me some time since I was waiting there anyway.  They let my kids come in and sit and watch (since they otherwise would have been unattended), and they entertained them while they waited.  They found the lost filling and repaired it in about 15 minutes.  Fantastic experience!< /Review>

First of all I have to say I am VERY impressed with the manager, Tom. I called in a To-Go order on a busy Sun. morning, when I called back later to say "Thank you" Tom recognized my voice & even remembered my name! He was very upbeat & made it a JOY to order from him :) (Also kudos to him because I assume he was manning the front because they were down a staff member, & doing a great job!). I ordered my eggs over-medium & bacon crispy, I was worried my egg whites might still be slimy & I'd have to re-cook the bacon also. But not at all! I'm pregnant & was really craving this, so I could not be more happy right now :)) Previously I chose to stay the heck away from Denny's (for about 8 yrs!) due to several negative experiences years ago at a diff. location, I won't say exactly what the last straw was because it's gross, but basically there was something in my food that shouldn't have been there :( So you can imagine my apprehensiveness about eating at any Denny's. Since visiting this location 3-4 times my trust in Denny's (at least this location) is fully restored! Every time we go the servers are upbeat & polite making it an enjoyable dining experience, & I've been pretty impressed with the food being cooked to order as well. Lastly it's a nice atmosphere, I don't know if they re-did it or maybe there was a steakhouse there previously & they kept the design/ deco., but it's a very nice setting as well. This location has turned me into a Happy HaPpY customer, very nice establishment :))) Thank you Tom & staff at Placerville Denny's!!!</text>
